{\footnotesize\ttfamily int ft\+\_\+add\+\_\+separator (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{fort_8h_a6307d2840e0e96880c4d0f04b12a2187}{ft\+\_\+table\+\_\+t}} $\ast$}]{table }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Erase range of cells.

Range of cells is determined by 2 points (top-\/left and bottom-\/right) (both ends are included).

{\footnotesize\ttfamily int ft\+\_\+nwrite (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{fort_8h_a6307d2840e0e96880c4d0f04b12a2187}{ft\+\_\+table\+\_\+t}} $\ast$}]{table,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{count,  }\item[{const char $\ast$}]{cell\+\_\+content,  }\item[{}]{... }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Write specified number of strings to the table.

Write specified number of strings to the same number of consecutive cells in the current row.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
In most cases it is more preferable to use MACRO \mbox{\hyperlink{fort_8h_aeb1059360e481caef1d2dcced5d5b646}{ft\+\_\+write}} instead of \mbox{\hyperlink{fort_8h_a69052e887e05d6dc3a0891550127619b}{ft\+\_\+nwrite}}, which is more safe (\mbox{\hyperlink{fort_8h_aeb1059360e481caef1d2dcced5d5b646}{ft\+\_\+write}} automatically counts the number of string arguments and at compile check that all passed arguments are strings).
\end{DoxyNote}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Paramètres}
{\em table} & Pointer to formatted table. \\
\hline
{\em count} & Number of strings to write. \\
\hline
{\em cell\+\_\+content} & First string to write. \\
\hline
{\em ...} & Other strings to write. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Renvoie}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 0\+: Success; data were written
\item ($<$0)\+: In case of error 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyReturn}

Write specified number of strings to the table and go to the next line.

Write specified number of strings to the same number of consecutive cells in the current row and move current position to the first cell of the next line(row).

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
In most cases it is more preferable to use MACRO \mbox{\hyperlink{fort_8h_aeb1059360e481caef1d2dcced5d5b646}{ft\+\_\+write}} instead of \mbox{\hyperlink{fort_8h_a69052e887e05d6dc3a0891550127619b}{ft\+\_\+nwrite}}, which is more safe (\mbox{\hyperlink{fort_8h_aeb1059360e481caef1d2dcced5d5b646}{ft\+\_\+write}} automatically counts the number of string arguments and at compile check that all passed arguments are strings).
\end{DoxyNote}

{\em table} & Pointer to formatted table. \\
\hline
{\em count} & Number of strings to write. \\
\hline
{\em cell\+\_\+content} & First string to write. \\
\hline
{\em ...} & Other strings to write. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyItemize}

\item ($<$0)\+: In case of error 
\end{DoxyItemize}

\index{fort.c@{fort.c}!ft\_set\_u8strwid\_func@{ft\_set\_u8strwid\_func}}
\index{ft\_set\_u8strwid\_func@{ft\_set\_u8strwid\_func}!fort.c@{fort.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ft\_set\_u8strwid\_func()}{ft\_set\_u8strwid\_func()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void ft\+\_\+set\+\_\+u8strwid\+\_\+func (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int($\ast$)(const void $\ast$beg, const void $\ast$end, size\+\_\+t $\ast$width)}]{u8strwid }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Set custom function to compute visible width of UTF-\/8 string.

libfort internally has a very simple logic to compute visible width of UTF-\/8 strings. It considers that each codepoint will occupy one position on the terminal in case of monowidth font (some east asians wide and fullwidth characters (see \href{http://www.unicode.org/reports/tr11/tr11-33.html}{\texttt{ http\+://www.\+unicode.\+org/reports/tr11/tr11-\/33.\+html}}) will occupy 2 positions). This logic is very simple and covers wide range of cases. But obviously there a lot of cases when it is not sufficient. In such cases user should use some external libraries and provide an appropriate function to libfort.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Paramètres}
{\em u8strwid} & User provided function to evaluate width of UTF-\/8 string ( beg -\/ start of UTF-\/8 string, end -\/ end of UTF-\/8 string (not included), width -\/ pointer to the result). If function succeed it should return 0, otherwise some non-\/ zero value. If function returns nonzero value libfort fallbacks to default internal algorithm. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{fort_8c_a50aacda85487577f3d84b3733134c660}\label{fort_8c_a50aacda85487577f3d84b3733134c660}}

\index{fort.c@{fort.c}!ft\_to\_string@{ft\_to\_string}}
\index{ft\_to\_string@{ft\_to\_string}!fort.c@{fort.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ft\_to\_string()}{ft\_to\_string()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily const char$\ast$ ft\+\_\+to\+\_\+string (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{fort_8h_a6307d2840e0e96880c4d0f04b12a2187}{ft\+\_\+table\+\_\+t}} $\ast$}]{table }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Convert table to string representation.

ft\+\_\+table\+\_\+t has ownership of the returned pointer. So there is no need to free it. To take ownership user should explicitly copy the returned string with strdup or similar functions.

Returned pointer may be later invalidated by\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Calling ft\+\_\+destroy\+\_\+table;
\item Other invocations of ft\+\_\+to\+\_\+string.
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyParams}{Paramètres}
{\em table} & Formatted table. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Renvoie}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item The pointer to the string representation of formatted table, on success.
\item NULL on error. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyReturn}
